  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_745e68d3-809a-474e-9273-08493c99f29d'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer13094966986470878271">Taran is an Assistant Pig-Keeper no longer; he has become a hero. Now he dreams of winning the hand of the Princess Eilonwy. Eager to find his origins, Taran sets off with the faithful Gurgi on a quest across the marvelous land of Prydain. Their journey takes them to the three witches in the Marshes of Morva, through the many realms of Prydain, and finally to the mystical </span>
  <span id="freeText13094966986470878271" style="display:none">Taran is an Assistant Pig-Keeper no longer; he has become a hero. Now he dreams of winning the hand of the Princess Eilonwy. Eager to find his origins, Taran sets off with the faithful Gurgi on a quest across the marvelous land of Prydain. Their journey takes them to the three witches in the Marshes of Morva, through the many realms of Prydain, and finally to the mystical Mirror of Llunet, which may hold a truth about Taran's identity that he cannot bear to face. In the course of his travels, Taran will learn much about his world and the good and bad people in it, but will also discover much about himself. <br /><br />After many hard lessons, Taran learns the secret of the Mirror Llunet and of the past--and finds not an ending but a beginning.</span>

          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {

<div id="review_1788160463" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1788160463" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8836060-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487160141p2/8836060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1788160463?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/8836060-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/7060522-taran-wanderer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8836060-michelle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8836060-michelle?shelf=for-kids-and-kidults">for-kids-and-kidults</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8836060-michelle?shelf=prydain">prydain</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1788160463" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer488151052768853372">My personal favorite in “The Chronicles of Prydain” is, no contest, “Taran Wanderer”. It doesn’t have a whole lot of swashbuckling action and gallantry, but as I've reread the books through the years, I've come to see it as the key to the series, and what lifts it into the realm of classics. The core of this series has always been Taran’s growth from a somewhat foolish and hapless boy into a man, and with each consecutive book he learns a little more about himself and the world around him. This </span>
  <span id="freeText488151052768853372" style="display:none">My personal favorite in “The Chronicles of Prydain” is, no contest, “Taran Wanderer”. It doesn’t have a whole lot of swashbuckling action and gallantry, but as I've reread the books through the years, I've come to see it as the key to the series, and what lifts it into the realm of classics. The core of this series has always been Taran’s growth from a somewhat foolish and hapless boy into a man, and with each consecutive book he learns a little more about himself and the world around him. This is the book in which he fully steps into manhood.<br /><br />With the intention to ask Princess Elionwy to marry him when she returns from her training on the Isle of Mona, Taran desires to learn more about his heritage. Having never known his parents, he harbors a secret wish that he has noble-blood in his veins; and so he sets out to discover the identity of his parents, and find his place in the world. On his travels he learns of the mysterious Mirror of Llunet which is said to show the true self of anyone who stares into it. With this as his somewhat vague goal, he heads out into the world. What follows is not so much a single overarching story, but a series of encounters and problems which Taran has to solve with his wit, compassion, bravery, common sense, and only occasionally his physical strength. From feuding lords to evil wizards, lawless mercenaries to the lessons of forge, loom and potter’s wheel -- each life experience leads him closer to who he really is.<br /> <br />As the story goes along, Lloyd Alexander also finds time to, subtly and wisely, add commentary on the human condition. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Taran comes up against the amorality of an outlaw, the injustice of a warlord, the arrogance of a wizard, and the simple dishonesty of a shepherd, and yet never relinquishes his own integrity, even as he faces fear, shame, and bitter disappointment. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But it’s not all doom and gloom. There’s plenty of room for humor, wonder and hope, usually obtained in the presence of Taran’s beloved companions: faithful Gurgi, the wandering bard Fflewdur Fflam, the grouchy dwarf Doli and the mischievous talking-crow Kaw .<br /> <br />Another aspect worthy of note is that Prydain itself is explored in more detail than in the previous books. While we’ve previously dealt with castles and princes, warlords and enchanters, we now get a look into the more humble - and more important - inhabitants of this imaginary world. The reader learns much from the simplest of folk including kindness to animals, respect to elders, the beauty of nature, and the simple pleasures of good food and a warm hearth. Knowing of their lives and their potential sacrifices makes the impact of the events to come more significant and tragic.<br /><br />The mythic hero always grows into adulthood in the process of fulfilling his or her destiny, but seldom has the process been heavier, more tinged with regret, more earned than in Taran's story. At its conclusion, all the pieces are in place for the final installment in this series, “The High King”, and lends its climactic events an immense emotional heft.<br /><br />My review for the whole series can be found here: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2794777699?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="488151052768853372" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7025819469315463511">The Book of Three (The Chronicles of Prydain, #4), Lloyd Alexander <br/>The Book of Three (1964) is a high fantasy novel by Lloyd Alexander, the first of five volumes in The Chronicles of Prydain. The series follows the adventures of Taran the Assistant Pig-Keeper, a youth raised by Dallben the enchanter, as he nears manhood while helping to resist the forces of Arawn Death-Lord. In 2012 The Book of Three was ranked number 18 among all-time best children's novels in a survey published by School Libra</span>
  <span id="freeText7025819469315463511" style="display:none">The Book of Three (The Chronicles of Prydain, #4), Lloyd Alexander <br />The Book of Three (1964) is a high fantasy novel by Lloyd Alexander, the first of five volumes in The Chronicles of Prydain. The series follows the adventures of Taran the Assistant Pig-Keeper, a youth raised by Dallben the enchanter, as he nears manhood while helping to resist the forces of Arawn Death-Lord. In 2012 The Book of Three was ranked number 18 among all-time best children's novels in a survey published by School Library Journal, a monthly with primarily U.S. audience. The concluding novel, The High King, was also among the top 100.<br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: بیست و چهارم ماه آگوست سال 2008 میلادی<br />عنوان: افسانه های پریداین - کتاب 4 - تاران و آینه ی مرموز؛ نویسنده: لوید الکساندر؛ مترجم: مریم سیادت؛ تهران، تندیس، 1385؛ در 272 ص؛ شابک: 9789648944174؛ <br />جلد چهام نیز عنوان اصلی اش «تاران سرگشته» بوده که در برگردان فارسی عنوان «تاران و آیینه مرموز» برای آن انتخاب شده است، سری پنج جلدی «افسانه‌های پرید‌این» د‌ر د‌هه‌ ی 60 قرن بیستم میلاد‌ی برای نخستین بار در ایالات متحده به چاپ رسید‌ه، به نوشته ی مهتاب روشنگران: «لین کارتر»، منتقد‌ مهم اد‌بیات فانتزی، از قول نویسنده سری «ماجراهای پریداین» نقل می‌کند‌، که جد‌ا از اثرپذیری ایشان از «تالکین»، کار او ملهم از کتابِ مهم د‌یگری د‌ر اد‌بیات فانتزیِ قرن بیستم میلادی، یعنی «شمشیر د‌ر سنگ» نیز هست (کتابی که به افسانه‌ های «آرتور شاه» می‌پرد‌ازد‌). همین مهم باعث شد‌ه تا سری «پرید‌این»، علاوه بر د‌اشتن المان‌های فانتزی بزرگسال، به طنز و شوخ و شنگی فانتزی‌های نوجوان هم نزد‌یک بشود‌. ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_367457336" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/367457336" />
    <a title="Michelle Isenhoff" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5319195-michelle-isenhoff"><img alt="Michelle Isenhoff" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556827290p2/5319195.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/367457336?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle Isenhoff" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle Isenhoff" href="/user/show/5319195-michelle-isenhoff">Michelle Isenhoff</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer367457336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5459188329390745352">“Who am I?”<br/><br/>That is the question Taran seeks to answer in book four of the Chronicles of Prydain. Taran has already had many adventures, fought many foes, won several battles, and fallen in love with Princess Eilonwy. He is held in high esteem by all who know him, yet he is still an Assistant Pig-Keeper, an orphan with no known history. Were his parents peasants, or could he be of noble blood, making him worthy of the princess? This is what he seeks to learn, and he covers all of Prydain in his q</span>
  <span id="freeText5459188329390745352" style="display:none">“Who am I?”<br /><br />That is the question Taran seeks to answer in book four of the Chronicles of Prydain. Taran has already had many adventures, fought many foes, won several battles, and fallen in love with Princess Eilonwy. He is held in high esteem by all who know him, yet he is still an Assistant Pig-Keeper, an orphan with no known history. Were his parents peasants, or could he be of noble blood, making him worthy of the princess? This is what he seeks to learn, and he covers all of Prydain in his quest.<br /><br />This book at first seemed a little pointless. There was no evil to defeat, no plot to foil. Taran simply began wandering with no clear direction and no clues to help him. “What I seek, I do not know. But, alas, I know it is not here.” But the old crew soon joins him—Gurgi, Doli and Ffluddur Flam—and the adventures start rolling in. The book grows as rich as ever, with the most important battle being waged inside Taran. It is exquisitely written. Once again I have page after page of notes, beautiful quotations, and nuggets of wisdom that give such deep insights into life. I just love this series.<br /><br />In his travels, Taran is offered King Smoit’s kingdom and refuses it. He’s offered a stone of power by the wizard Morda and refuses it. He shows excellent leadership abilities, he judges disputes with the wisdom of King Solomon, he repays friendship with aid, he inspires courage and displays loyalty. In every respect, he acts admirably and proves himself noble. Before his quest ends (I won’t tell you if he’s nobly born or not), he realizes the folly of looking to blood to prove one’s worth: “When I was a child I dreamed of adventure, glory of honor in feats of arms. I think now that these things are shallow….As for my parentage, it makes little difference…manhood is not given but earned.”<br /><br />Here are a few more quotes that I really like:<br /><br />“Once the apple is ripe, no man can turn it back to a greening.”<br /><br />“Was a royal robe enough to hide a dishonorable deed?”<br /><br />“If I fret over tomorrow, I’ll have little joy today.”<br /><br />“Trust your luck, Taran Wanderer, but don’t forget to put out your net.”<br /><br />“Craftsmanship isn’t like water in an earthen pot, to be taken out by the dipperful until it’s empty. No, the more drawn out the more remains.”<br /><br />“Life is clay to be shaped.”<br /><br />Though I have not looked at the final book in the series, I believe this one sets it up in some important ways. As a result of his journey, Taran has established relationships all over Prydain, he’s learned the hardships its people face, and he’s seen how Arawn, the evil Lord, has devastated the land. He has also gathered a great deal of experience, wisdom and confidence. I believe in the next book, The High King, that Taran will face Arawn in a final battle and emerge as the leader of all Prydain. He has certainly proved himself able. I also think the princess Eilonwy will make a significant return to the series. I missed her fiery personality in this one.<br /><br />Though I can make some strong predictions as to the tale’s ending, I wouldn’t miss the reading of it. This series has been phenomenal. Truly the sweetest of adventures! I’m off to purchase the last book now…</span>
  <a data-text-id="5459188329390745352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2468101468347399127" style="display:none">Nice coming of age story that marks a change from the other books in the series. I'd say it was reasonably free standing, but then I'm the kind of person who regards starting watching a film from the middle as a challenge rather than an impediment. Here the adopted Taran wants to find out about himself and has a series of adventures culminating in accepting himself without having to have noble ancestors to make life worth living.<br /><br />The journey towards this destination is made up by a <i>Wanderjahr</i> round part of Alexander's Prydain - a mythical version of ancient Wales complete with it's own wizard and little people who live underground. <br /><br />On his journey the young Taran tries out various professions from sheep herder, to potter, to blacksmith, to weaver. On being confronted with the idea that weaving is woman's work the old woman who is the master weaver points out that she had never heard a job complain about who did it. Experience has shown this to be very true. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the gender politics of the rest of the series is less exciting with women appearing as mothers, wives, a wicked witch and the three fates. Although the magical prophetic pig is a sow - there you go, a broader view of gender achieved one pig at a time. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />The traditional triple goddesses who in these books literally weave the fates of mice and men, creating an inconveniently long comic strip version of what we read remind me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Where%20ever%20you%20go,%20there%20you%20are" title=" Where ever you go, there you are" rel="nofollow noopener"> Where ever you go, there you are</a> because unlike the rest of us who cannot ever take a break from being ourselves and forever carry the consequences of our actions in ourselves for good and ill they swap bodies and personalities amongst each other, unfortunately since one of the three is distinctly sour tempered and perpetually irritable this has to be strictly regulated and the poor goddess has to be obliged to be herself whether she likes it or not, which naturally results in her being more than normally sour and irritable like a person eating fresh sloes<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ if you haven't tried it, don't.         rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4307906-michael-sorbello?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4307906-michael-sorbello?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2788856836" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3911313450098122272">Struggling to find a sense of purpose in the world, Taran separates from his crew to do a bit of soul searching. He searches for his noble or common lineage in the eastern regions of Prydain, far from both the realm and forces of Arawn and the demesne of the High King. Along the way, he meets many people, learns new skills and crafts, and confronts some rough characters.<br/><br/>The direction of the plot had trouble catching my attention at first, but the entire second half of the book was the best mater</span>
  <span id="freeText3911313450098122272" style="display:none">Struggling to find a sense of purpose in the world, Taran separates from his crew to do a bit of soul searching. He searches for his noble or common lineage in the eastern regions of Prydain, far from both the realm and forces of Arawn and the demesne of the High King. Along the way, he meets many people, learns new skills and crafts, and confronts some rough characters.<br /><br />The direction of the plot had trouble catching my attention at first, but the entire second half of the book was the best material that I’ve gotten to experience from this series by far. Compared to the last three books, it was incredibly mature and full of complex human emotions. I was fascinated to watch Taran become a man and win over my respect after having mixed feelings about him for so long. I thought he was a terrible character when the series first started, yet now he’s someone I can look up to with genuine respect and sympathy. <br /><br />From unlikable brat to honorable warrior, a boy that has outgrown his insecurities regarding his low status and unknown origins and learned to accept himself for what he is. Taran is all grown up and he’s destined to accomplish great things. I feel like every book in this series has been much better than the last, I hope that the fifth and final installment will blow me away even more than this one.<br /><br />***<br /><br />My Social Media<br /><br />My Instagram Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/michael_sorbello/">https://www.instagram.com/michael_sor...</a><br /><br />My Wattpad Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.wattpad.com/user/Michael-Sorbello">https://www.wattpad.com/user/Michael-...</a><br /><br />My YouTube Channel: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCPPs1eOzsOqcz5ey5JjGSbg">https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCPPs...</a><br /><br />My Twitter Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/SorbelloHorror">https://twitter.com/SorbelloHorror</a><br /><br />My Facebook Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/michael.sorbello.104">https://www.facebook.com/michael.sorb...</a></span>

<div id="review_2231779072" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2231779072" />
    <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos"><img alt="Sotiris Karaiskos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407195235p2/18940246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2231779072?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sotiris Karaiskos" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos">Sotiris Karaiskos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12471219-taran-wanderer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2231779072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3357067397319123794">The fourth part of the series is, as the author writes in his foreword, the most heroic of all. In this, our beloved pig keeper begins a journey to discover his true origin so that he can stand next to his beloved as an equal. In this journey, we follow the classic pattern of fairy tales and mythological circles, with the hero encountering difficulties, obstacles, dangerous people and overcoming them with his power and wit. Of course, on this trip he meets people who give him valuable advice and</span>
  <span id="freeText3357067397319123794" style="display:none">The fourth part of the series is, as the author writes in his foreword, the most heroic of all. In this, our beloved pig keeper begins a journey to discover his true origin so that he can stand next to his beloved as an equal. In this journey, we follow the classic pattern of fairy tales and mythological circles, with the hero encountering difficulties, obstacles, dangerous people and overcoming them with his power and wit. Of course, on this trip he meets people who give him valuable advice and help him on his way. Following the same pattern, the journey is essentially a way of shaping the character, acquiring the necessary skills and in our case a passage from childhood to adulthood. And of course, as in most journeys, it is understood that the issue is not the destination but the journey itself.<br /><br /> In other words, we have before us the deepest and most philosophical book of the series so far. A book that includes many important lessons that are not limited to the young audience to which it is addressed. Of course, as in the previous parts of this series, it does not mean that it's not fun enough to be attractive, it just gives the reader much more food for thought. Shortly before the end, I feel that I have read another important book that matters even more when I think of how positive effect it can have in shaping the character of children.<br /><br /> Το τέταρτο μέρος της σειράς είναι, όπως λέει και ο συγγραφέας στον πρόλογο του, το πιο ηρωικό από όλα. Σε αυτό ο αγαπητός μας χοιροβοσκός ξεκινάει ένα ταξίδι για να ανακαλύψει την πραγματική καταγωγή του ώστε να μπορεί να σταθεί δίπλα στην αγαπημένη του ως ίσος. Σε αυτό το ταξίδι ακολουθούμε το κλασικό μοτίβο των παραμυθιών και των μυθολογικών κύκλων, με τον ήρωα να συναντά στο δρόμο του δυσκολίες, εμπόδια, επικίνδυνους ανθρώπους και να τα βγάζει πέρα με τη δύναμη και την εξυπνάδα του. Φυσικά σε αυτό το ταξίδι συναντά και ανθρώπους που του δίνουν πολύτιμες συμβουλές και τον βοηθάνε στη διαδρομή του. Ακολουθώντας το ίδιο μοτίβο το ταξίδι γίνεται ουσιαστικά μία διαδρομή διαμόρφωσης του χαρακτήρα, απόκτησης των απαραίτητων εφοδίων και στην περίπτωσή μας του περάσματος από την παιδική ηλικία στην ενηλικίωση. Και φυσικά όπως και στα περισσότερα ταξίδια γίνεται αντιληπτό ότι το ζήτημα δεν είναι ο προορισμός αλλά το ίδιο το ταξίδι.<br /><br /> Με άλλα λόγια έχουμε μπροστά μας το πιο βαθύ και το πιο φιλοσοφημένο βιβλίο της σειράς ως τώρα. Ένα βιβλίο που περιλαμβάνει πολλά σημαντικά διδάγματα που δεν περιορίζονται μόνο στο νεανικό κοινό στο οποίο απευθύνεται. Φυσικά όπως και στα προηγούμενα μέρη της σειράς αυτό δεν σημαίνει ότι το ίδιο δεν είναι αρκετά διασκεδαστικό για να είναι ελκυστικό, απλά δίνει στον αναγνώστη πολύ περισσότερη τροφή για σκέψη. Λίγο πριν το τέλος, δηλαδή, νιώθω ότι διάβασα άλλο ένα σημαντικό βιβλίο που η σημασία του γίνεται ακόμα μεγαλύτερη όταν σκέφτομαι πόσο θετική επίδραση μπορεί να έχει στη διαμόρφωση των παιδιών.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3357067397319123794" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1240859373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8147776291030626982"><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478991849i/21137618.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>“True allegiance is only given willingly.”<br/>
</blockquote><br/>Having discovered his feelings for the Princess Eilonwy, Taran, now more than ever, longs to know his parentage. Travelling through all corners of Prydain, his quest leads him to farmers and kings - yet from none can he learn who he truly is. <br/><br/>Unlike the previous instalments, <b>Taran Wanderer</b> does not focus on any particular evil that must be met. In a way, Taran is his own enemy as he, almost aimlessly, travels from place to place. It gives the book a mo</span>
  <span id="freeText8147776291030626982" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478991849i/21137618.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>“True allegiance is only given willingly.”<br>
</blockquote><br>Having discovered his feelings for the Princess Eilonwy, Taran, now more than ever, longs to know his parentage. Travelling through all corners of Prydain, his quest leads him to farmers and kings - yet from none can he learn who he truly is. <br><br>Unlike the previous instalments, <b>Taran Wanderer</b> does not focus on any particular evil that must be met. In a way, Taran is his own enemy as he, almost aimlessly, travels from place to place. It gives the book a more quiet nature and has an almost melancholic feeling to it.<br><br>Although a more calm book, when it comes down to it, Taran faces some fierce battles that are shown in more detail than in any of the previous books. That being said, it might be because Taran faces them one on one rather than the author trying to describe a large battle altogether. In any case, although it only held a few, this book's action scenes were nicely written. <br><br>For the most of it, only Gurgi accompanies Taran throughout the quest. Fflewdurr does make quite a prominent appearance (and I'm sure glad of that) and we get to see Doli for a couple of chapters. Although I missed seeing some of the other characters (such as Eilonwy) it gave more room for Taran's character development - and that turned out to be great!<br><br>I've liked Taran from book one and I grow fonder of him with every new instalment. He is a character who constantly learns. His temper can still get the better of him but he will always learn a lesson or two from his mistaken judgments. <br><br>Gurgi is, as always, such a faithful and lovable companion. This book, more than any of the others, showed how loyal he truly is - Taran's journey would have been a lonely one without him. <br><br>I love how this book dealt with one's self-perception. It shows that no matter who your parents are, you are who you choose to be and it is in your own hands to shape your life. Although already a solid character, Taran has learnt and grown a lot during this quest!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8147776291030626982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6199178702202444933" style="display:none">This is my favorite of the five books. Somewhat seasoned by his previous adventures, Taran sets off to find out who he is. Like so many, he thinks his parentage has something to do with it. He's offered some easy answers, but continues to look &amp; in the process meets some interesting people &amp; learns several crafts. He learns them well enough to learn the basics &amp; that he doesn't have the calling to master them. <br /><br />Best of all, he learns that a simple bit of iron, cloth, or clay pot isn't simple at all. He's raised sheep &amp; sheared them &amp; finds that turning that fleece into a cloak is an arduous task taking more strength, stamina, time, &amp; skill than he would have believed. It's a great lesson &amp; one that I've learned myself. (I was spinning some alpaca fleece into thread as I listened to this. Several bobbins worth have to be spun before I can ply it together into yarn that I'll then knit or crochet into a 'simple' hat or scarf.)<br /><br />He learns a lot more besides, but that would be a spoiler. The book was a fast, intriguing read, so I'm off to listen to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24781.The_High_King__The_Chronicles_of_Prydain__5_" title="The High King (The Chronicles of Prydain #5) by Lloyd Alexander" rel="nofollow noopener">The High King</a> to finish these up.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1623577615112569243">This is the moment where Taran, and this series, grows up. <br/><br/>Taran Wanderer is a wondrous book, and I enjoyed it immensely. I can understand, however, why children (or adults) who adored the first three books in the Prydain series may be thrown off by it, as it doesn't really follow the same path as the others.   <span id="freeText1623577615112569243" style="display:none">This is the moment where Taran, and this series, grows up. <br /><br />Taran Wanderer is a wondrous book, and I enjoyed it immensely. I can understand, however, why children (or adults) who adored the first three books in the Prydain series may be thrown off by it, as it doesn't really follow the same path as the others. As the title suggests, Taran (and subsequently the reader) are wandering for the majority of the story. This is also by far the darkest book yet in the series.<br /><br />After the events in The Castle of Llyr, Taran now knows two things: 1) He is in love with Princess Eilonwy, and 2) He can only marry her if he is nobly born. As he has never known his true parents, there is a part of him that wonders if perhaps they WERE noble. He sets off with Gurgi to discover who he really is.<br /><br />And that is all I will say. Taran has many adventures throughout this book, but the most captivating aspect of it for me was how deftly Lloyd Alexander handles Taran's pursuit to discover himself. The ending of this book is not EPIC, but poignant and full of wisdom. <br /><br />I can't wait to finish the series! Highly recommended.</span>

<div id="review_2046854492" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2046854492" />
    <a title="Joaquin Mejia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60598412-joaquin-mejia"><img alt="Joaquin Mejia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520158003p2/60598412.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2046854492?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joaquin Mejia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joaquin Mejia" href="/user/show/60598412-joaquin-mejia">Joaquin Mejia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2046854492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8875059803522724419">Since I did not get to write reviews for the previous books of "The Chronicles of Prydain" I think I will have to explain a little bit of the story. This series of five books follows a young man called Taran who really wants to be a hero. He dreams of glory, honor, and adventure. But he realizes that heroism is not easy. He learns it the hard way through his adventures in the fantasy land of kings, queens, princes, and princesses called Prydain where he encounters things both wondrous and terrib</span>
  <span id="freeText8875059803522724419" style="display:none">Since I did not get to write reviews for the previous books of "The Chronicles of Prydain" I think I will have to explain a little bit of the story. This series of five books follows a young man called Taran who really wants to be a hero. He dreams of glory, honor, and adventure. But he realizes that heroism is not easy. He learns it the hard way through his adventures in the fantasy land of kings, queens, princes, and princesses called Prydain where he encounters things both wondrous and terrible. This is the fourth book of Lloyd Alexander's children's series and I thought it was a very good book. But I think I liked the predecessors a bit more.<br /><br /> This book is about Taran's quest for his identity. He wants to marry Princess Eilonwy and he feels that he would only be worthy of marrying her if he was a descendant of kings. This lead him on a quest for the Mirror of Llunet which people say can show the true identity of any person who looks at it. He is accompanied by his usual companions( with the exception of Princess Eilonwy) in his adventure but it would later turn into aimless wandering. Like in his previous adventures, Taran would learn a lot of lessons.<br /><br /> This book is unique in the series because it has less royalty in it. This book seems to take our attention away from the kings and queens and to the common people. The best part about this is that Taran learns just as much lessons from the farmers,weavers,potters, artisans, and shepherds as he does from the princes and wizards. Many of the wise words that Alexander puts in this book come from the common people who don't live in castles or cast magical spells. The author always said that his fantasy world is really no different from the real world despite its magic. Could it be that this book is about the wisdom of ordinary people like our co-workers, classmates, or members of our family? Maybe it is. I think many people are like Taran, dreaming of heroism and glory, but easily forget that there is much greatness and wisdom in the people they see everyday. Let's not forget that even the most ordinary people can teach us great lessons.<br /><br /> So I am going to move onto the fifth and final book of this series. The last book won a Newbery Medal so I will really expect it to be very good. But I already know that Lloyd Alexander is a very great writer. Anyone can learn a lot from his books. I hope more people, especially children, will read his books. They will have a lot of fun reading them but they will, like Taran, also learn a lot as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8875059803522724419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer1148903275938191802">I liked this story the least of the Prydain Chronicles. It's important to the series because it shows Taran really understanding that his identity is based on his ability and accomplishments rather than on position; however, I missed Eilonwy who is barely in it and I found myself not becoming attached to the new characters as much. I didn't think there was enough dynamic. Mostly Taran is being mentored and there isn't as much tension as characters, interact with each other. The story reads more </span>
  <span id="freeText1148903275938191802" style="display:none">I liked this story the least of the Prydain Chronicles. It's important to the series because it shows Taran really understanding that his identity is based on his ability and accomplishments rather than on position; however, I missed Eilonwy who is barely in it and I found myself not becoming attached to the new characters as much. I didn't think there was enough dynamic. Mostly Taran is being mentored and there isn't as much tension as characters, interact with each other. The story reads more like a folktale with clear morals or lessons Taran learns from his mentors. The usual humor exists and there are action scenes; however the character dynamics didn't hold my interest cover to cover. I didn't burn any meals because I couldn't put this book down.<br /><br />Taran goes on a quest to discover his parentage so that he can marry Eilonwy. He fantasizes that he is the son of a king and queen and he journeys to far away lands in search of his roots. He gains wisdom and learns how to negotiate and settle disputes by listening to two nobles who are fighting. His ability to empathize with others is a leadership quality that he keeps honing. He continues to learn to rely on himself versus magic and it is his raw honesty with himself and reflections of who he is that makes him so accessible and endearing to the reader. When he is fooled over his parentage, rather than getting angry with the wrong-doer, he realizes that part of the fault lay within himself as well. He realized he had to set aside his shame of not being of noble birth. <br /><br />On his travels, he meets many common people and learns the nobleness of everyday work. It is after he is apprenticed to a weaver, metal-smith, potter, and farmer that he realizes actions determine what defines a person and not ancestry. When he travels to the Mirror of Llunt, the self-revelation that he has good and bad inside of him helps him accept his orphan status and ignoble birth. He is no longer ashamed and gains wisdom to be content with his station in life.<br /><br />While learning skilled crafts, Taran learns what it means to fail and not be good at something because he doesn't have a passion for it. One of the journey's with growing up is trying to find something one has a passion for or is good at in life. Taran explores this concept and also realizes that he has a limitation when it comes to making pottery. He does not have the greatness within to be like the master potter he is under. This is a powerful message because to be happy in a chosen profession, a person must have a passion for it, as well as some natural bent. I liked the messages in this book, I just struggled with the pacing in parts. And I missed Eilonwy ; )</span>
  <a data-text-id="1148903275938191802" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_971020006" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/971020006" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597876967p2/1343864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/971020006?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780881030952" href="/book/show/728034.Taran_Wanderer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=heroes-and-villains">heroes-and-villains</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=kid-lit">kid-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=orphalins">orphalins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=treasure-and-adventure">treasure-and-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=bildungsroman">bildungsroman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=award-winners">award-winners</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer971020006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7360831121245536806">In terms of character development, <i>Taran Wanderer</i> is probably the most impressive of the five Chronicles of Prydain books.<br/><br/>There is no evil to overcome in this one, no one wrong to right, no one to rescue. Taran simply wants to know where he came from, and so he sets off from Caer Dallben with only Gurgi and his faithful steed Melynlass to accompany him and no idea of where to start looking for the secrets to his heritage. Of course, Taran also has some other motives going on here. Mostly he want</span>
  <span id="freeText7360831121245536806" style="display:none">In terms of character development, <i>Taran Wanderer</i> is probably the most impressive of the five Chronicles of Prydain books.<br /><br />There is no evil to overcome in this one, no one wrong to right, no one to rescue. Taran simply wants to know where he came from, and so he sets off from Caer Dallben with only Gurgi and his faithful steed Melynlass to accompany him and no idea of where to start looking for the secrets to his heritage. Of course, Taran also has some other motives going on here. Mostly he wants to know where he came from because he wants to be worthy of the Princess Eilonwy, because everyone knows only a man of noble birth can marry a princess. He knows deep down that he very well might find he is a person of no consequence, but a very large part of him does in fact expect to find out he's some secret prince, or the long lost son of lord.<br /><br />As Taran doesn't know where to start looking, he goes to the only people in Prydain who might be able to point him in the right direction: the enchantresses Orddu, Orwen, and Orgach. After a bit of flim-flammery and misdirection, they tell him there is a mirror that if looked upon will show him who he truly is. And so Taran and Gurgi set off to find the Mirror of Llunet. Their journey, however, is quickly and frequently derailed by chance meetings, scuffles with local lords, and a crisis of confidence-inducing encounter with a sheep farmer in the Northern Commets, among other things. Every encounter Taran has (some with familiar faces like King Smoit and Fflewddur Fflam) leaves his preconceptions about the world and himself changed, shifted, or even erased. He learns more about himself in the looking than in the finding, as the three enchantresses had warned him.<br /><br />What was really interesting to me is that all of the encounters Taran has seem specifically tailored by Alexander into shaping Taran as a man. He sees many examples of leadership and masculinity in his year of travels (I joked in a status update on Goodreads that everyone in this book either wanted to kill or adopt him), which enables him to see the type of man he is becoming, and examine whether that is someone he should aspire to be at all. The almost bleak nature of the questions the book asks of Taran frankly astounded me in places (I'm thinking particularly of his encounter with Craddoc the Shepherd). And the ending doesn't go where you think it's going to go, considering the premise.<br /><br />If I ever have a son, he's definitely getting these books as a present one day--you know, as like, a hint. Just really great stuff here.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7360831121245536806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_321295683" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/321295683" />
    <a title="Courtney H." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4276947-courtney-h"><img alt="Courtney H." src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/321295683?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Courtney H." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Courtney H." href="/user/show/4276947-courtney-h">Courtney H.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer321295683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13988266699388084337">I really enjoyed Taran Wanderer. Taran grew up quite a bit, which made him more fun to read as a protagonist. I really liked the characters that Alexander introduced. Some were nuanced; some were merely Good (like the people of the Free Commots), but still likeable and for once not bumbling, if still somewhat whimsical. <br/><br/>This book follows Taran as he quests for his parentage. Alexander introduces us to some of his most nuanced, interesting characters yet, such as Craddoc; and Taran himself grows </span>
  <span id="freeText13988266699388084337" style="display:none">I really enjoyed Taran Wanderer. Taran grew up quite a bit, which made him more fun to read as a protagonist. I really liked the characters that Alexander introduced. Some were nuanced; some were merely Good (like the people of the Free Commots), but still likeable and for once not bumbling, if still somewhat whimsical. <br /><br />This book follows Taran as he quests for his parentage. Alexander introduces us to some of his most nuanced, interesting characters yet, such as Craddoc; and Taran himself grows a great deal. Old friends return; we get two new bad guys, one of whom is still alive to provide foil in book 5; and we get the people of the Free Commots, a collection of villages not under any kingdom, who govern themselves. Taran spends a great deal of time there, learning from their artisans and forming strong relationships that will carry through the end of the series. I liked Llonio best, but they were all marvelous (if clearly there to help Taran grow). <br /><br />The pacing of this book was better than the last. The book does not get bogged down anywhere, and Alexander puts Taran through quite a few trials, to help in grow and keep us, as readers, entertained. Of course, this--like so many penultimate books--is largely a set up for what is coming: the big war. Bumbling won't do when it comes down to it, so Taran had to grow up and become effective, as did many characters; he had to start forming relationships from which he might command loyalty; we have to get a sense of the full landscape of Prydain, so as to understand how the various factions and geography will affect the war. Alexander set it up well, and this was a very satisfying book to bring us toward the conclusion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13988266699388084337" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2104805659123433970">The fourth book in the Chronicles of Prydain. Taran, despairing that he will ever know himself, leaves Caer Dallben with Gurgi to find the Mirror of Llunet, which will show himself as he truly is. Taran meets greedy cantrev lords, aids a generous king, is taken captive by a mad wizard, and apprentices himself to a smith, a weaver, and a potter.<br/><br/>In some ways, this is the weakest of the books, being a series of only occasionally suspenseful events, with little in the way on conflict or climax, and </span>
  <span id="freeText2104805659123433970" style="display:none">The fourth book in the Chronicles of Prydain. Taran, despairing that he will ever know himself, leaves Caer Dallben with Gurgi to find the Mirror of Llunet, which will show himself as he truly is. Taran meets greedy cantrev lords, aids a generous king, is taken captive by a mad wizard, and apprentices himself to a smith, a weaver, and a potter.<br /><br />In some ways, this is the weakest of the books, being a series of only occasionally suspenseful events, with little in the way on conflict or climax, and that being of the very simplistic kind. But while Alexander is cramming the Archetypical Quest to Become a Man into a slim children’s volume, his always very fine writing carries the book along, and the inner growth of Taran is a fine lesson for children and young adults, who are on the same quest. <br /><br />[Read twice]</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15925856579978234432">Best of the series so far. Easily. Taran is growing up and so is the series. This story reads like a little like a fable, even while holding many of the same fantasy journey elements of the previous three installments. The last few chapters were exceptionally perfect, and I personally think that the chapter titled "The Weir" is one of the favorite pieces of literature I've read recently. I have a feeling that others might feel the same way about one of the other encounters before or after. And t</span>
  <span id="freeText15925856579978234432" style="display:none">Best of the series so far. Easily. Taran is growing up and so is the series. This story reads like a little like a fable, even while holding many of the same fantasy journey elements of the previous three installments. The last few chapters were exceptionally perfect, and I personally think that the chapter titled "The Weir" is one of the favorite pieces of literature I've read recently. I have a feeling that others might feel the same way about one of the other encounters before or after. And that's what makes this book special. It feels like more than just a good sequel, but an exploration of what it takes and what it means to find yourself.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10675172967821759535">Taran gets some time off from saving his friends or detroying evil artifacts, and decides to spend that time to go on a personal quest of discovery, finding out more about himself and what his place in the world might be.   <span id="freeText10675172967821759535" style="display:none">Taran gets some time off from saving his friends or detroying evil artifacts, and decides to spend that time to go on a personal quest of discovery, finding out more about himself and what his place in the world might be. There's not much at stake, world-wise: it's all very personal and down-to-earth and, with a cast of new and colorful characters, works great enough. Taran learns a lot, but also shows himself pretty clever from the beginning.<br /><br />Well-written, tense, often funny, but I miss Eilonwy - and I can forgive even that, since it's her very existence that still gets the plot going to begin with. <div id="review_2421527432" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2421527432" />
    <a title="Eustacia Tan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6609117-eustacia-tan"><img alt="Eustacia Tan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553435967p2/6609117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2421527432?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eustacia Tan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eustacia Tan" href="/user/show/6609117-eustacia-tan">Eustacia Tan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2421527432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15777425895242371760">Like I mentioned in my review of The Castle of Llyr, I borrowed the remaining books of the Prydain series as soon as I could. Unfortunately, I couldn’t get The Foundling and other Tales of Prydain, but at least I got the last two books of the series!<br/><br/>In Taran Wanderer, Taran decides to leave Caer Dallben and search for this true parentage. Well, the truth is that he’s hoping to find out he’s of noble parentage so that he can ask Eilonwy for her hand in marriage. And so, Taran and Gurgi wander thr</span>
  <span id="freeText15777425895242371760" style="display:none">Like I mentioned in my review of The Castle of Llyr, I borrowed the remaining books of the Prydain series as soon as I could. Unfortunately, I couldn’t get The Foundling and other Tales of Prydain, but at least I got the last two books of the series!<br /><br />In Taran Wanderer, Taran decides to leave Caer Dallben and search for this true parentage. Well, the truth is that he’s hoping to find out he’s of noble parentage so that he can ask Eilonwy for her hand in marriage. And so, Taran and Gurgi wander through the land, meeting people and having adventures.<br /><br />Truth be told, I thought that this was the weakest book in the Chronicles of Prydain series so far. While Taran does have a quest to find out his parentage, much of the book reads like a series of loosely connected adventures rather than a story with an overarching focus.<br /><br />That said, there are plenty of great moments in the book, especially in the second half of the story. Taran starts to learn about the true value of things and he starts to see that his original goal of hoping for noble blood isn’t what he thought he was. And as he wanders through the land and tries his hand at different skills, he also learns more about who he isn’t - an important lesson for everyone as they try to figure out who they are.<br /><br />For me, the character that really shone in this book (even more than Taran) was Gurgi. Gurgi was introduced as an odd creature who is cowardly. And though Gurgi retains his old manner of speaking, I’ve noticed that he has really grown in courage and loyalty - it is no small feat to keep following Taran around. I find that this is the book where I really start to appreciate Gurgi as a character.<br /><br />Overall, while this wasn’t as strong as the other books in the series, it still has a lot to offer. Taran’s journey of trying out different things mimics what a lot of us will do, and I think the lesson of learning to try things that may not work out is a valuable one for everyone reading it.<br /><br />This review was first posted at <a href="http://allsortsofbooks.blogspot.com/2018/06/taran-wanderer-by-lloyd-alexander.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Inside the mind of a Bibliophile</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15777425895242371760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1837649851" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1837649851" />
    <a title="Devyn Duffy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15916140-devyn-duffy"><img alt="Devyn Duffy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587860616p2/15916140.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1837649851?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Devyn Duffy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Devyn Duffy" href="/user/show/15916140-devyn-duffy">Devyn Duffy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone except very young children</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Devyn by: </span>
      my fourth-grade English teacher
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1837649851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7110377104796751593">"I've never heard the work complain of who did it, so long as it got done!"<br/><br/>Taran Wanderer, the fourth book in the five-book Prydain Chronicles series, has been my favorite since I first read it as a fourth-grader. While half of the story is adventure in the face of grave danger like in the other books, the other half of the story is more human and real.<br/><br/>Taran is now old enough to realize that it's OK to admit that he likes a girl. Unfortunately, Eilonwy is a princess and is away at princess schoo</span>
  <span id="freeText7110377104796751593" style="display:none">"I've never heard the work complain of who did it, so long as it got done!"<br /><br />Taran Wanderer, the fourth book in the five-book Prydain Chronicles series, has been my favorite since I first read it as a fourth-grader. While half of the story is adventure in the face of grave danger like in the other books, the other half of the story is more human and real.<br /><br />Taran is now old enough to realize that it's OK to admit that he likes a girl. Unfortunately, Eilonwy is a princess and is away at princess school (so to speak), so the Assistant Pig-Keeper Taran believes that he must discover that he is of noble birth himself to be worthy of proposing marriage to her, and Eilonwy isn't around to talk him out of the idea. Much of this book's story, then, is Taran's quest to discover who his parents were, and to find out who he is now.<br /><br />Unlike other fantasy stories, however, the search isn't straightforward and there's no cryptic prophecy to guide the characters. Most of Taran's search for identity is instead a quest to create an identity, by going from place to place, meeting various people, and learning what he can from them. And much of what he does is useful work for people of modest means: farming, smithing, pottery-making, and more. It's in these moments, when Taran is learning or developing his skills with an experienced teacher while no one is trying to kill him, that this book really shines. And each teacher has his or her own personality and point of view, giving Taran and the reader the chance to choose which lessons are best worth remembering.<br /><br />Like the other books, the pacing is fast even when months go by. While a chapter or two might be too intense for very young children, the danger never lasts long. And also like the other books, this one can be read on its own but is much more powerful when read in sequence. I only wish that in fourth grade I had realized that Taran's lessons would have been just as valuable for me--this would be a good book for adults to read along with children and discuss afterward.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7110377104796751593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4605349740477218835">I really liked this book. It, along with The Black Cauldron, is probably my favorite in the series so far.<br/><br/>Taran Wanderer focuses entirely on Taran as he struggles to find out where he comes from and who his parents are. It is uniquely written, as each chapter covers (more or less) one leg of his journey, as he confronts some problem, learns from it, and continues his journey. It is very satisfying to see Taran do things right and succeed in everything he does through his own wit, rather than bei</span>
  <span id="freeText4605349740477218835" style="display:none">I really liked this book. It, along with The Black Cauldron, is probably my favorite in the series so far.<br /><br />Taran Wanderer focuses entirely on Taran as he struggles to find out where he comes from and who his parents are. It is uniquely written, as each chapter covers (more or less) one leg of his journey, as he confronts some problem, learns from it, and continues his journey. It is very satisfying to see Taran do things right and succeed in everything he does through his own wit, rather than being the sort of bumbling, lucky, follower that he is in the earliest books in the series.<br /><br />It is also very interesting how Taran continuously finds places where he admits he would be happy to spend the rest of his days, but continues on in order to achieve his greater goal, of finding out who he is.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4004414534895503472">That is some deep stuff. In the fourth book of Prydain Chronicles Taran realizes that he loves Princess Eilowny (who is again missing from the narrative) and goes on a journey of self-discovery. He hopes to be of noble birth, so he can propose marriage to the princess, thinking that an assistant pig-keeper would not be worthy of her hand. What he gets though is a lesson in self-worth, societal prejudices, and misconceptions about human nature. Can facilitate some great philosophical discussions </span>
  <span id="freeText4004414534895503472" style="display:none">That is some deep stuff. In the fourth book of Prydain Chronicles Taran realizes that he loves Princess Eilowny (who is again missing from the narrative) and goes on a journey of self-discovery. He hopes to be of noble birth, so he can propose marriage to the princess, thinking that an assistant pig-keeper would not be worthy of her hand. What he gets though is a lesson in self-worth, societal prejudices, and misconceptions about human nature. Can facilitate some great philosophical discussions with your kid. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4004414534895503472" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WWr67gP4KTvGa2jvBXMQ5KzyS1mApyaGlW72qvsOw7lNZyhc0Ouu8EqSBxFB7b8T4xRiQTUllfpwhq1JuvwK4A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('N6oWjt8bQYTwdVbsDc9FaRFFIdtdQ8A6wB9sAQnw0eojp8Q8DAjGT3yMORJJUeqeXqMIw+jBc0Yl9zfiSAIYsw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

The adventures of Alice-named for one of the little girls to whom the book was dedicated-who journeys down a rabbit hole and into a whimsical underworld realm instantly struck a chord with the British public, and then with readers around the world. In 1872, in reaction to the universal acclaim *Alice\'s Adventures in Wonderland* received, Dodgson published this sequel. Nothing is quite what it seems once Alice journeys through the looking-glass, and Dodgson\'s wit is infectious as he explores concepts of mirror imagery, time running backward, and strategies of chess-all wrapped up in the exploits of a spirited young girl who parries with the Red Queen, Tweedledee and Tweedledum, and other unlikely characters. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13452023714624913534"><b>Lloyd Chudley Alexander</b> was an influential American author of more than forty books, mostly fantasy novels for children and adolescents, as well as several adult books. His most famous contribution to the field of children's literature is the fantasy series <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/40371-the-chronicles-of-prydain' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Chronicles of Prydain</a>. The concluding book of the series, <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24781.The_High_King' title='The High King' rel='nofollow noopener'>The High King</a>
</i>, was awarded the Newbery Medal in 1969. Alexander's other book</span>
  <span id="freeText13452023714624913534" style="display:none"><b>Lloyd Chudley Alexander</b> was an influential American author of more than forty books, mostly fantasy novels for children and adolescents, as well as several adult books. His most famous contribution to the field of children's literature is the fantasy series <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40371-the-chronicles-of-prydain" rel="nofollow noopener">The Chronicles of Prydain</a>. The concluding book of the series, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24781.The_High_King" title="The High King" rel="nofollow noopener">The High King</a>
</i>, was awarded the Newbery Medal in 1969. Alexander's other books have also won the National Book Award and the American Book Award. He was also one of the creators of <i>Cricket Magazine.</i></span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/2628-taran-wanderer">Quotes from Taran Wanderer</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Life's a forge! Yes, and hammer and anvil, too! You'll be roasted, smelted, and pounded, and you'll scarce know what's happening to you. But stand boldly to it! Metal's worthless till it's shaped and tempered! More labor than luck. Face the pounding, don't fear the proving; and you'll stand well against any hammer and anvil.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/96335-life-s-a-forge-yes-and-hammer-and-anvil-too-you-ll">95 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Llonio said life was a net for luck; to Hevydd the Smith life was a forge; and to Dwyvach the Weaver-Woman a loom. They spoke truly, for it is all of these. But you,' Taran said, his eyes meeting the potter's, 'you have shown me life is one thing more. It is clay to be shaped, as raw clay on a potter's wheel.&rdquo;</span>
